At application startup, passes are registered\n// with the PassRegistry, which is later provided to the PassManager for\n// dependency resolution and similar tasks.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n#define LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/RWMutex.h\"\n#include <memory>\n#include <vector>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass PassInfo;\nstruct PassRegistrationListener;\n\n/// PassRegistry - This class manages the registration and intitialization of\n/// the pass subsystem as application startup, and assists the PassManager\n/// in resolving pass dependencies.\n/// NOTE: PassRegistry is NOT thread-safe.  If you want to use LLVM on multiple\n/// threads simultaneously, you will need to use a separate PassRegistry on\n/// each thread.\nclass PassRegistry {\n  mutable sys::SmartRWMutex<true> Lock;\n\n  /// PassInfoMap - Keep track of the PassInfo object for each registered pass.\n  using MapType = DenseMap<const void *, const PassInfo *>;\n  MapType PassInfoMap;\n\n  using StringMapType = StringMap<const PassInfo *>;\n  StringMapType PassInfoStringMap;\n\n  std::vector<std::unique_ptr<const PassInfo>> ToFree;\n  std::vector<PassRegistrationListener *> Listeners;\n\npublic:\n  PassRegistry() = default;\n  LLVM_ABI ~PassRegistry();\n\n  /// getPassRegistry - Access the global registry object, which is\n  /// automatically initialized at application launch and destroyed by\n  /// llvm_shutdown.\n  LLVM_ABI static PassRegistry *getPassRegistry();\n\n  /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\n  /// type identifier (&MyPass::ID).\n  LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(const void *TI) const;\n\n  /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\n  /// argument string.\n  LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(StringRef Arg) const;\n\n  /// registerPass - Register a pass (by means of its PassInfo) with the\n  /// registry.  Required in order to use the pass with a PassManager.\n  LLVM_ABI void registerPass(const PassInfo &PI, bool ShouldFree = false);\n\n  /// enumerateWith - Enumerate the registered passes, calling the provided\n  /// PassRegistrationListener's passEnumerate() callback on each of them.\n  LLVM_ABI void enumerateWith(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n\n  /// addRegistrationListener - Register the given PassRegistrationListener\n  /// to receive passRegistered() callbacks whenever a new pass is registered.\n  LLVM_ABI void addRegistrationListener(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n\n  /// removeRegistrationListener - Unregister a PassRegistrationListener so that\n  /// it no longer receives passRegistered() callbacks.\n  LLVM_ABI void removeRegistrationListener(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n};\n\n} // end namespace llvm\n\n#endif // LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n","numLines":88,"startLine":1,"totalLines":88}}}

This allows arbitrary passes to be strung together and have them\n    15→// executed as efficiently as possible.\n    16→//\n    17→// Passes should extend one of the classes below, depending on the guarantees\n    18→// that it can make about what will be modified as it is run.  For example, most\n    19→// global optimizations should derive from FunctionPass, because they do not add\n    20→// or delete functions, they operate on the internals of the function.\n    21→//\n    22→// Note that this file #includes PassSupport.h and PassAnalysisSupport.h (at the\n    23→// bottom), so the APIs exposed by these files are also automatically available\n    24→// to all users of this file.\n    25→//\n    26→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    27→\n    28→#ifndef LLVM_PASS_H\n    29→#define LLVM_PASS_H\n    30→\n    31→#ifdef EXPENSIVE_CHECKS\n    32→#include <cstdint>\n    33→#endif\n    34→#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n    35→#include <string>\n    36→\n    37→namespace llvm {\n    38→\n    39→class AnalysisResolver;\n    40→class AnalysisUsage;\n    41→class Function;\n    42→class ImmutablePass;\n    43→class Module;\n    44→class PassInfo;\n    45→class PMDataManager;\n    46→class PMStack;\n    47→class raw_ostream;\n    48→class StringRef;\n    49→\n    50→// AnalysisID - Use the PassInfo to identify a pass...\n    51→using AnalysisID = const void *;\n    52→\n    53→/// Different types of internal pass managers. External pass managers\n    54→/// (PassManager and FunctionPassManager) are not represented here.\n    55→/// Ordering of pass manager types is important here.\n    56→enum PassManagerType {\n    57→  PMT_Unknown = 0,\n    58→  PMT_ModulePassManager = 1, ///< MPPassManager\n    59→  PMT_CallGraphPassManager,  ///< CGPassManager\n    60→  PMT_FunctionPassManager,   ///< FPPassManager\n    61→  PMT_LoopPassManager,       ///< LPPassManager\n    62→  PMT_RegionPassManager,     ///< RGPassManager\n    63→  PMT_Last\n    64→};\n    65→\n    66→// Different types of passes.\n    67→enum PassKind {\n    68→  PT_Region,\n    69→  PT_Loop,\n    70→  PT_Function,\n    71→  PT_CallGraphSCC,\n    72→  PT_Module,\n    73→  PT_PassManager\n    74→};\n    75→\n    76→/// This enumerates the LLVM full LTO or ThinLTO optimization phases.\n    77→enum class ThinOrFullLTOPhase {\n    78→  /// No LTO/ThinLTO behavior needed.\n    79→  None,\n    80→  /// ThinLTO prelink (summary) phase.\n    81→  ThinLTOPreLink,\n    82→  /// ThinLTO postlink (backend compile) phase.\n    83→  ThinLTOPostLink,\n    84→  /// Full LTO prelink phase.\n    85→  FullLTOPreLink,\n    86→  /// Full LTO postlink (backend compile) phase.\n    87→  FullLTOPostLink\n    88→};\n    89→\n    90→#ifndef NDEBUG\n    91→const char *to_string(ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n    92→#endif\n    93→\n    94→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    95→/// Pass interface - Implemented by all 'passes'.  Subclass this if you are an\n    96→/// interprocedural optimization or you do not fit into any of the more\n    97→/// constrained passes described below.\n    98→///\n    99→class LLVM_ABI Pass {\n   100→  AnalysisResolver *Resolver = nullptr;  // Used to resolve analysis\n   101→  const void *PassID;\n   102→  PassKind Kind;\n   103→\n   104→public:\n   105→  explicit Pass(PassKind K, char &pid) : PassID(&pid), Kind(K) {}\n   106→  Pass(const Pass &) = delete;\n   107→  Pass &operator=(const Pass &) = delete;\n   108→  virtual ~Pass();\n   109→\n   110→  PassKind getPassKind() const { return Kind; }\n   111→\n   112→  /// getPassName - Return a nice clean name for a pass.  This usually\n   113→  /// implemented in terms of the name that is registered by one of the\n   114→  /// Registration templates, but can be overloaded directly.\n   115→  virtual StringRef getPassName() const;\n   116→\n   117→  /// Return a nice clean name for a pass\n   118→  /// corresponding to that used to enable the pass in opt.\n   119→  StringRef getPassArgument() const;\n   120→\n   121→  /// getPassID - Return the PassID number that corresponds to this pass.\n   122→  AnalysisID getPassID() const {\n   123→    return PassID;\n   124→  }\n   125→\n   126→  /// doInitialization - Virtual method overridden by subclasses to do\n   127→  /// any necessary initialization before any pass is run.\n   128→  virtual bool doInitialization(Module &)  { return false; }\n   129→\n   130→  /// doFinalization - Virtual method overriden by subclasses to do any\n   131→  /// necessary clean up after all passes have run.\n   132→  virtual bool doFinalization(Module &) { return false; }\n   133→\n   134→  /// print - Print out the internal state of the pass.  This is called by\n   135→  /// Analyze to print out the contents of an analysis.  Otherwise it is not\n   136→  /// necessary to implement this method.  Beware that the module pointer MAY be\n   137→  /// null.  This automatically forwards to a virtual function that does not\n   138→  /// provide the Module* in case the analysis doesn't need it it can just be\n   139→  /// ignored.\n   140→  virtual void print(raw_ostream &OS, const Module *M) const;\n   141→\n   142→  void dump() const; // dump - Print to stderr.\n   143→\n   144→  /// createPrinterPass - Get a Pass appropriate to print the IR this\n   145→  /// pass operates on (Module, Function or MachineFunction).\n   146→  virtual Pass *createPrinterPass(raw_ostream &OS,\n   147→                                  const std::string &Banner) const = 0;\n   148→\n   149→  /// Each pass is responsible for assigning a pass manager to itself.\n   150→  /// PMS is the stack of available pass manager.\n   151→  virtual void assignPassManager(PMStack &,\n   152→                                 PassManagerType) {}\n   153→\n   154→  /// Check if available pass managers are suitable for this pass or not.\n   155→  virtual void preparePassManager(PMStack &);\n   156→\n   157→  ///  Return what kind of Pass Manager can manage this pass.\n   158→  virtual PassManagerType getPotentialPassManagerType() const;\n   159→\n   160→  // Access AnalysisResolver\n   161→  void setResolver(AnalysisResolver *AR);\n   162→  AnalysisResolver *getResolver() const { return Resolver; }\n   163→\n   164→  /// getAnalysisUsage - This function should be overriden by passes that need\n   165→  /// analysis information to do their job.  If a pass specifies that it uses a\n   166→  /// particular analysis result to this function, it can then use the\n   167→  /// getAnalysis<AnalysisType>() function, below.\n   168→  virtual void getAnalysisUsage(AnalysisUsage &) const;\n   169→\n   170→  /// releaseMemory() - This member can be implemented by a pass if it wants to\n   171→  /// be able to release its memory when it is no longer needed.  The default\n   172→  /// behavior of passes is to hold onto memory for the entire duration of their\n   173→  /// lifetime (which is the entire compile time).  For pipelined passes, this\n   174→  /// is not a big deal because that memory gets recycled every time the pass is\n   175→  /// invoked on another program unit.  For IP passes, it is more important to\n   176→  /// free memory when it is unused.\n   177→  ///\n   178→  /// Optionally implement this function to release pass memory when it is no\n   179→  /// longer used.\n   180→  virtual void releaseMemory();\n   181→\n   182→  virtual ImmutablePass *getAsImmutablePass();\n   183→  virtual PMDataManager *getAsPMDataManager();\n   184→\n   185→  /// verifyAnalysis() - This member can be implemented by a analysis pass to\n   186→  /// check state of analysis information.\n   187→  virtual void verifyAnalysis() const;\n   188→\n   189→  // dumpPassStructure - Implement the -debug-passes=PassStructure option\n   190→  virtual void dumpPassStructure(unsigned Offset = 0);\n   191→\n   192→  // lookupPassInfo - Return the pass info object for the specified pass class,\n   193→  // or null if it is not known.\n   194→  static const PassInfo *lookupPassInfo(const void *TI);\n   195→\n   196→  // lookupPassInfo - Return the pass info object for the pass with the given\n   197→  // argument string, or null if it is not known.\n   198→  static const PassInfo *lookupPassInfo(StringRef Arg);\n   199→\n   200→  // createPass - Create a object for the specified pass class,\n   201→  // or null if it is not known.\n   202→  static Pass *createPass(AnalysisID ID);\n   203→\n   204→  /// getAnalysisIfAvailable<AnalysisType>() - Subclasses use this function to\n   205→  /// get analysis information that might be around, for example to update it.\n   206→  /// This is different than getAnalysis in that it can fail (if the analysis\n   207→  /// results haven't been computed), so should only be used if you can handle\n   208→  /// the case when the analysis is not available.  This method is often used by\n   209→  /// transformation APIs to update analysis results for a pass automatically as\n   210→  /// the transform is performed.\n   211→  template<typename AnalysisType> AnalysisType *\n   212→    getAnalysisIfAvailable() const; // Defined in PassAnalysisSupport.h\n   213→\n   214→  /// mustPreserveAnalysisID - This method serves the same function as\n   215→  /// getAnalysisIfAvailable, but works if you just have an AnalysisID.  This\n   216→  /// obviously cannot give you a properly typed instance of the class if you\n   217→  /// don't have the class name available (use getAnalysisIfAvailable if you\n   218→  /// do), but it can tell you if you need to preserve the pass at least.\n   219→  bool mustPreserveAnalysisID(char &AID) const;\n   220→\n   221→  /// getAnalysis<AnalysisType>() - This function is used by subclasses to get\n   222→  /// to the analysis information that they claim to use by overriding the\n   223→  /// getAnalysisUsage function.\n   224→  template<typename AnalysisType>\n   225→  AnalysisType &getAnalysis() const; // Defined in PassAnalysisSupport.h\n   226→\n   227→  template <typename AnalysisType>\n   228→  AnalysisType &\n   229→  getAnalysis(Function &F,\n   230→              bool *Changed = nullptr); // Defined in PassAnalysisSupport.h\n   231→\n   232→  template<typename AnalysisType>\n   233→  AnalysisType &getAnalysisID(AnalysisID PI) const;\n   234→\n   235→  template <typename AnalysisType>\n   236→  AnalysisType &getAnalysisID(AnalysisID PI, Function &F,\n   237→                              bool *Changed = nullptr);\n   238→\n   239→#ifdef EXPENSIVE_CHECKS\n   240→  /// Hash a module in order to detect when a module (or more specific) pass has\n   241→  /// modified it.\n   242→  uint64_t structuralHash(Module &M) const;\n   243→\n   244→  /// Hash a function in order to detect when a function (or more specific) pass\n   245→  /// has modified it.\n   246→  virtual uint64_t structuralHash(Function &F) const;\n   247→#endif\n   248→};\n   249→\n   250→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n   251→/// ModulePass class - This class is used to implement unstructured\n   252→/// interprocedural optimizations and analyses.  ModulePasses may do anything\n   253→/// they want to the program.\n   254→///\n   255→class LLVM_ABI ModulePass : public Pass {\n   256→public:\n   257→  explicit ModulePass(char &pid) : Pass(PT_Module, pid) {}\n   258→\n   259→  // Force out-of-line virtual method.\n   260→  ~ModulePass() override;\n   261→\n   262→  /// createPrinterPass - Get a module printer pass.\n   263→  Pass *createPrinterPass(raw_ostream &OS,\n   264→                          const std::string &Banner) const override;\n   265→\n   266→  /// runOnModule - Virtual method overriden by subclasses to process the module\n   267→  /// being operated on.\n   268→  virtual bool runOnModule(Module &M) = 0;\n   269→\n   270→  void assignPassManager(PMStack &PMS, PassManagerType T) override;\n   271→\n   272→  ///  Return what kind of Pass Manager can manage this pass.\n   273→  PassManagerType getPotentialPassManagerType() const override;\n   274→\n   275→protected:\n   276→  /// Optional passes call this function to check whether the pass should be\n   277→  /// skipped. This is the case when optimization bisect is over the limit.\n   278→  bool skipModule(const Module &M) const;\n   279→};\n   280→\n   281→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n   282→/// ImmutablePass class - This class is used to provide information that does\n   283→/// not need to be run.  This is useful for things like target information.\n   284→///\n   285→class LLVM_ABI ImmutablePass : public ModulePass {\n   286→public:\n   287→  explicit ImmutablePass(char &pid) : ModulePass(pid) {}\n   288→\n   289→  // Force out-of-line virtual method.\n   290→  ~ImmutablePass() override;\n   291→\n   292→  /// initializePass - This method may be overriden by immutable passes to allow\n   293→  /// them to perform various initialization actions they require.  This is\n   294→  /// primarily because an ImmutablePass can \"require\" another ImmutablePass,\n   295→  /// and if it does, the overloaded version of initializePass may get access to\n   296→  /// these passes with getAnalysis<>.\n   297→  virtual void initializePass();\n   298→\n   299→  ImmutablePass *getAsImmutablePass() override { return this; }\n   300→\n   301→  /// ImmutablePasses are never run.\n   302→  bool runOnModule(Module &) override { return false; }\n   303→};\n   304→\n   305→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n   306→/// FunctionPass class - This class is used to implement most global\n   307→/// optimizations.  Optimizations should subclass this class if they meet the\n   308→/// following constraints:\n   309→///\n   310→///  1. Optimizations are organized globally, i.e., a function at a time\n   311→///  2. Optimizing a function does not cause the addition or removal of any\n   312→///     functions in the module\n   313→///\n   314→class LLVM_ABI FunctionPass : public Pass {\n   315→public:\n   316→  explicit FunctionPass(char &pid) : Pass(PT_Function, pid) {}\n   317→\n   318→  /// createPrinterPass - Get a function printer pass.\n   319→  Pass *createPrinterPass(raw_ostream &OS,\n   320→                          const std::string &Banner) const override;\n   321→\n   322→  /// runOnFunction - Virtual method overriden by subclasses to do the\n   323→  /// per-function processing of the pass.\n   324→  virtual bool runOnFunction(Function &F) = 0;\n   325→\n   326→  void assignPassManager(PMStack &PMS, PassManagerType T) override;\n   327→\n   328→  ///  Return what kind of Pass Manager can manage this pass.\n   329→  PassManagerType getPotentialPassManagerType() const override;\n   330→\n   331→protected:\n   332→  /// Optional passes call this function to check whether the pass should be\n   333→  /// skipped. This allows arbitrary passes to be strung together and have them\n// executed as efficiently as possible.\n//\n// Passes should extend one of the classes below, depending on the guarantees\n// that it can make about what will be modified as it is run.  For example, most\n// global optimizations should derive from FunctionPass, because they do not add\n// or delete functions, they operate on the internals of the function.\n//\n// Note that this file #includes PassSupport.h and PassAnalysisSupport.h (at the\n// bottom), so the APIs exposed by these files are also automatically available\n// to all users of this file.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_PASS_H\n#define LLVM_PASS_H\n\n#ifdef EXPENSIVE_CHECKS\n#include <cstdint>\n#endif\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include <string>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass AnalysisResolver;\nclass AnalysisUsage;\nclass Function;\nclass ImmutablePass;\nclass Module;\nclass PassInfo;\nclass PMDataManager;\nclass PMStack;\nclass raw_ostream;\nclass StringRef;\n\n// AnalysisID - Use the PassInfo to identify a pass...\nusing AnalysisID = const void *;\n\n/// Different types of internal pass managers. External pass managers\n/// (PassManager and FunctionPassManager) are not represented here.\n/// Ordering of pass manager types is important here.\nenum PassManagerType {\n  PMT_Unknown = 0,\n  PMT_ModulePassManager = 1, ///< MPPassManager\n  PMT_CallGraphPassManager,  ///< CGPassManager\n  PMT_FunctionPassManager,   ///< FPPassManager\n  PMT_LoopPassManager,       ///< LPPassManager\n  PMT_RegionPassManager,     ///< RGPassManager\n  PMT_Last\n};\n\n// Different types of passes.\nenum PassKind {\n  PT_Region,\n  PT_Loop,\n  PT_Function,\n  PT_CallGraphSCC,\n  PT_Module,\n  PT_PassManager\n};\n\n/// This enumerates the LLVM full LTO or ThinLTO optimization phases.\nenum class ThinOrFullLTOPhase {\n  /// No LTO/ThinLTO behavior needed.\n  None,\n  /// ThinLTO prelink (summary) phase.\n  ThinLTOPreLink,\n  /// ThinLTO postlink (backend compile) phase.\n  ThinLTOPostLink,\n  /// Full LTO prelink phase.\n  FullLTOPreLink,\n  /// Full LTO postlink (backend compile) phase.\n  FullLTOPostLink\n};\n\n#ifndef NDEBUG\nconst char *to_string(ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n#endif\n\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n/// Pass interface - Implemented by all 'passes'.  Subclass this if you are an\n/// interprocedural optimization or you do not fit into any of the more\n/// constrained passes described below.\n///\nclass LLVM_ABI Pass {\n  AnalysisResolver *Resolver = nullptr;  // Used to resolve analysis\n  const void *PassID;\n  PassKind Kind;\n\npublic:\n  explicit Pass(PassKind K, char &pid) : PassID(&pid), Kind(K) {}\n  Pass(const Pass &) = delete;\n  Pass &operator=(const Pass &) = delete;\n  virtual ~Pass();\n\n  PassKind getPassKind() const { return Kind; }\n\n  /// getPassName - Return a nice clean name for a pass.  This usually\n  /// implemented in terms of the name that is registered by one of the\n  /// Registration templates, but can be overloaded directly.\n  virtual StringRef getPassName() const;\n\n  /// Return a nice clean name for a pass\n  /// corresponding to that used to enable the pass in opt.\n  StringRef getPassArgument() const;\n\n  /// getPassID - Return the PassID number that corresponds to this pass.\n  AnalysisID getPassID() const {\n    return PassID;\n  }\n\n  /// doInitialization - Virtual method overridden by subclasses to do\n  /// any necessary initialization before any pass is run.\n  virtual bool doInitialization(Module &)  { return false; }\n\n  /// doFinalization - Virtual method overriden by subclasses to do any\n  /// necessary clean up after all passes have run.\n  virtual bool doFinalization(Module &) { return false; }\n\n  /// print - Print out the internal state of the pass.  This is called by\n  /// Analyze to print out the contents of an analysis.  Otherwise it is not\n  /// necessary to implement this method.  Beware that the module pointer MAY be\n  /// null.  This automatically forwards to a virtual function that does not\n  /// provide the Module* in case the analysis doesn't need it it can just be\n  /// ignored.\n  virtual void print(raw_ostream &OS, const Module *M) const;\n\n  void dump() const; // dump - Print to stderr.\n\n  /// createPrinterPass - Get a Pass appropriate to print the IR this\n  /// pass operates on (Module, Function or MachineFunction).\n  virtual Pass *createPrinterPass(raw_ostream &OS,\n                                  const std::string &Banner) const = 0;\n\n  /// Each pass is responsible for assigning a pass manager to itself.\n  /// PMS is the stack of available pass manager.\n  virtual void assignPassManager(PMStack &,\n                                 PassManagerType) {}\n\n  /// Check if available pass managers are suitable for this pass or not.\n  virtual void preparePassManager(PMStack &);\n\n  ///  Return what kind of Pass Manager can manage this pass.\n  virtual PassManagerType getPotentialPassManagerType() const;\n\n  // Access AnalysisResolver\n  void setResolver(AnalysisResolver *AR);\n  AnalysisResolver *getResolver() const { return Resolver; }\n\n  /// getAnalysisUsage - This function should be overriden by passes that need\n  /// analysis information to do their job.  If a pass specifies that it uses a\n  /// particular analysis result to this function, it can then use the\n  /// getAnalysis<AnalysisType>() function, below.\n  virtual void getAnalysisUsage(AnalysisUsage &) const;\n\n  /// releaseMemory() - This member can be implemented by a pass if it wants to\n  /// be able to release its memory when it is no longer needed.  The default\n  /// behavior of passes is to hold onto memory for the entire duration of their\n  /// lifetime (which is the entire compile time).  For pipelined passes, this\n  /// is not a big deal because that memory gets recycled every time the pass is\n  /// invoked on another program unit.  For IP passes, it is more important to\n  /// free memory when it is unused.\n  ///\n  /// Optionally implement this function to release pass memory when it is no\n  /// longer used.\n  virtual void releaseMemory();\n\n  virtual ImmutablePass *getAsImmutablePass();\n  virtual PMDataManager *getAsPMDataManager();\n\n  /// verifyAnalysis() - This member can be implemented by a analysis pass to\n  /// check state of analysis information.\n  virtual void verifyAnalysis() const;\n\n  // dumpPassStructure - Implement the -debug-passes=PassStructure option\n  virtual void dumpPassStructure(unsigned Offset = 0);\n\n  // lookupPassInfo - Return the pass info object for the specified pass class,\n  // or null if it is not known.\n  static const PassInfo *lookupPassInfo(const void *TI);\n\n  // lookupPassInfo - Return the pass info object for the pass with the given\n  // argument string, or null if it is not known.\n  static const PassInfo *lookupPassInfo(StringRef Arg);\n\n  // createPass - Create a object for the specified pass class,\n  // or null if it is not known.\n  static Pass *createPass(AnalysisID ID);\n\n  /// getAnalysisIfAvailable<AnalysisType>() - Subclasses use this function to\n  /// get analysis information that might be around, for example to update it.\n  /// This is different than getAnalysis in that it can fail (if the analysis\n  /// results haven't been computed), so should only be used if you can handle\n  /// the case when the analysis is not available.  This method is often used by\n  /// transformation APIs to update analysis results for a pass automatically as\n  /// the transform is performed.\n  template<typename AnalysisType> AnalysisType *\n    getAnalysisIfAvailable() const; // Defined in PassAnalysisSupport.h\n\n  /// mustPreserveAnalysisID - This method serves the same function as\n  /// getAnalysisIfAvailable, but works if you just have an AnalysisID.  This\n  /// obviously cannot give you a properly typed instance of the class if you\n  /// don't have the class name available (use getAnalysisIfAvailable if you\n  /// do), but it can tell you if you need to preserve the pass at least.\n  bool mustPreserveAnalysisID(char &AID) const;\n\n  /// getAnalysis<AnalysisType>() - This function is used by subclasses to get\n  /// to the analysis information that they claim to use by overriding the\n  /// getAnalysisUsage function.\n  template<typename AnalysisType>\n  AnalysisType &getAnalysis() const; // Defined in PassAnalysisSupport.h\n\n  template <typename AnalysisType>\n  AnalysisType &\n  getAnalysis(Function &F,\n              bool *Changed = nullptr); // Defined in PassAnalysisSupport.h\n\n  template<typename AnalysisType>\n  AnalysisType &getAnalysisID(AnalysisID PI) const;\n\n  template <typename AnalysisType>\n  AnalysisType &getAnalysisID(AnalysisID PI, Function &F,\n                              bool *Changed = nullptr);\n\n#ifdef EXPENSIVE_CHECKS\n  /// Hash a module in order to detect when a module (or more specific) pass has\n  /// modified it.\n  uint64_t structuralHash(Module &M) const;\n\n  /// Hash a function in order to detect when a function (or more specific) pass\n  /// has modified it.\n  virtual uint64_t structuralHash(Function &F) const;\n#endif\n};\n\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n/// ModulePass class - This class is used to implement unstructured\n/// interprocedural optimizations and analyses.  ModulePasses may do anything\n/// they want to the program.\n///\nclass LLVM_ABI ModulePass : public Pass {\npublic:\n  explicit ModulePass(char &pid) : Pass(PT_Module, pid) {}\n\n  // Force out-of-line virtual method.\n  ~ModulePass() override;\n\n  /// createPrinterPass - Get a module printer pass.\n  Pass *createPrinterPass(raw_ostream &OS,\n                          const std::string &Banner) const override;\n\n  /// runOnModule - Virtual method overriden by subclasses to process the module\n  /// being operated on.\n  virtual bool runOnModule(Module &M) = 0;\n\n  void assignPassManager(PMStack &PMS, PassManagerType T) override;\n\n  ///  Return what kind of Pass Manager can manage this pass.\n  PassManagerType getPotentialPassManagerType() const override;\n\nprotected:\n  /// Optional passes call this function to check whether the pass should be\n  /// skipped. This is the case when optimization bisect is over the limit.\n  bool skipModule(const Module &M) const;\n};\n\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n/// ImmutablePass class - This class is used to provide information that does\n/// not need to be run.  This is useful for things like target information.\n///\nclass LLVM_ABI ImmutablePass : public ModulePass {\npublic:\n  explicit ImmutablePass(char &pid) : ModulePass(pid) {}\n\n  // Force out-of-line virtual method.\n  ~ImmutablePass() override;\n\n  /// initializePass - This method may be overriden by immutable passes to allow\n  /// them to perform various initialization actions they require.  This is\n  /// primarily because an ImmutablePass can \"require\" another ImmutablePass,\n  /// and if it does, the overloaded version of initializePass may get access to\n  /// these passes with getAnalysis<>.\n  virtual void initializePass();\n\n  ImmutablePass *getAsImmutablePass() override { return this; }\n\n  /// ImmutablePasses are never run.\n  bool runOnModule(Module &) override { return false; }\n};\n\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n/// FunctionPass class - This class is used to implement most global\n/// optimizations.  Optimizations should subclass this class if they meet the\n/// following constraints:\n///\n///  1. Optimizations are organized globally, i.e., a function at a time\n///  2. There\n/// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n/// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n/// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n/// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n/// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n/// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n/// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n/// single module provided.\n///\n/// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n/// modules and functions.\n///\n/// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n///   a Function.\n/// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n///\n/// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n/// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n/// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n/// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n/// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n/// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\n/// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\n///\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n#define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/TinyPtrVector.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstring>\n#include <list>\n#include <memory>\n#include <tuple>\n#include <type_traits>\n#include <utility>\n#include <vector>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass Function;\nclass Module;\n\n// Forward declare the analysis manager template.\ntemplate <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\n\n/// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\n/// passes.\n///\n/// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\ntemplate <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\n  /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\n  static StringRef name() {\n    static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n                  \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n    StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\n    Name.consume_front(\"llvm::\");\n    return Name;\n  }\n\n  void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\n                     function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\n    StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\n    auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\n    OS << PassName;\n  }\n};\n\n/// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\n///\n/// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\n/// automatically mixes in \\c PassInfoMixin.\ntemplate <typename DerivedT>\nstruct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\n  /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\n  ///\n  /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\n  /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\n  /// bits of pointers.\n  ///\n  /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\c AnalysisKey\n  /// member called \\c Key.\n  ///\n  /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\n  /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\n  /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\n  /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\n  /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\n  /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\n  static AnalysisKey *ID() {\n    static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n                  \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n    return &DerivedT::Key;\n  }\n};\n\nnamespace detail {\n\n/// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\n/// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\ntemplate <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\n          typename... ArgTs, size_t... Ns>\ntypename PassT::Result\ngetAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n                             std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\n                             std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\n  (void)Args;\n  return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\n}\n\n/// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\n///\n/// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\n/// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\n/// pass to getResult.\ntemplate <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... AnalysisArgTs,\n          typename... MainArgTs>\ntypename PassT::Result\ngetAnalysisResult(AnalysisManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisArgTs...> &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n                  std::tuple<MainArgTs...> Args) {\n  return (getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple<\n          PassT, IRUnitT>)(AM, IR, Args,\n                           std::index_sequence_for<AnalysisArgTs...>{});\n}\n\n} // namespace detail\n\n/// Manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR.\n///\n/// A pass manager contains a sequence of passes to run over a particular unit\n/// of IR (e.g. Functions, Modules). It is itself a valid pass over that unit of","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":965}}}

registration through execution order in the O2/O3 optimization pipeline.\\n\\n## Registration Phase\\nPasses are registered via the PassSupport.h macros. The RegisterPass<> template (llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h:89) is the primary mechanism for registering new passes. This template creates a PassInfo object describing the pass and registers it with the global PassRegistry via PassRegistry::registerPass() (llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h:70). The INITIALIZE_PASS macro (llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h:56-58) provides an alternative mechanism for passes with dependencies, using once_flag synchronization to initialize passes exactly once.\\n\\nPassRegistry (llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h) maintains two maps: PassInfoMap (indexed by pass type ID) and PassInfoStringMap (indexed by pass argument names). This allows lookup by either the pass pointer address or the string name used on the command line.\\n\\n## PassManager Template and Structure\\nThe core PassManager template is defined in llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h:159-226. It is a template class parameterized by IRUnitT (Module, Function, etc.) and an AnalysisManagerT. The PassManager stores passes as a vector of PassConceptT pointers (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h:225), implementing concept-based polymorphism to allow heterogeneous pass types.\\n\\nSpecialized typedefs are provided:\\n- ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module> (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h:238)\\n- FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function> (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h:247)\\n\\nThe addPass() method (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h:193-214) accepts any pass type and wraps it in a PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...> object before storing it. This allows passes of different types to be added to the same manager.\\n\\n## Pass Execution Order\\nPass execution happens in PassManager::run() (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerImpl.h:28-98). The method iterates through the stored passes sequentially (line 67: for (auto &Pass : Passes)). For each pass:\\n\\n1. PassInstrumentation::runBeforePass() callbacks are invoked (line 73)\\n2. The pass's run() method is called with the IR unit and AnalysisManager (line 76)\\n3. The AnalysisManager invalidates analyses based on the pass's PreservedAnalyses result (line 80)\\n4. PassInstrumentation::runAfterPass() callbacks are invoked (line 84)\\n5. Preserved analyses are intersected across all passes (line 88)\\n\\nThis sequential execution ensures dependency ordering and analysis invalidation consistency.\\n\\n## O2/O3 Optimization Pipeline Construction\\nThe PassBuilder class (llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h and llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilder.cpp) constructs the optimization pipeline. The entry point for standard optimizations is buildModuleOptimizationPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase LTOPhase) defined in llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp:1478.\\n\\nThis function:\\n1. This pipeline is invoked within the module pipeline to process each function.\\n\\n## Pass Registration Database\\nPassRegistry.def (llvm/lib/Passes/PassRegistry.def) defines all registered passes using MODULE_PASS, CGSCC_PASS, and FUNCTION_PASS macros. Each entry specifies the pass creation expression, enabling dynamic pass creation by the PassBuilder.\\n\\n## Analysis Management and Dependencies\\nAnalysisManager (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h:249+) caches analysis results and manages pass dependencies. This template creates a PassInfo object describing the pass and registers it with the global PassRegistry via PassRegistry::registerPass() (llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h:70). The INITIALIZE_PASS macro (llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h:56-58) provides an alternative mechanism for passes with dependencies, using once_flag synchronization to initialize passes exactly once.\\n\\nPassRegistry (llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h) maintains two maps: PassInfoMap (indexed by pass type ID) and PassInfoStringMap (indexed by pass argument names). This allows passes of different types to be added to the same manager.\\n\\n## Pass Execution Order\\nPass execution happens in PassManager::run() (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerImpl.h:28-98).
